   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Merle Haggard</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>

     <p><span class="error" style="display:none">HIDDEN ERROR: Usage of "cause_of_death" is not recognized</span></p> 
     <p><b>Merle Ronald Haggard</b> (April 6, 1937&nbsp;– April 6, 2016) was an American <a href="/wiki/Singer" title="Singer" class="mw-redirect">singer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Songwriter" title="Songwriter">songwriter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guitarist" title="Guitarist">guitarist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fiddler" title="Fiddler" class="mw-redirect">fiddler</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Instrumentalist" title="Instrumentalist" class="mw-redirect">instrumentalist</a>. Along with <a href="/wiki/Buck_Owens" title="Buck Owens">Buck Owens</a>, Haggard and his band <a href="/wiki/The_Strangers_(American_band)" title="The Strangers (American band)">the Strangers</a> helped create the <a href="/wiki/Bakersfield_sound" title="Bakersfield sound">Bakersfield sound</a>, which is characterized by the twang of <a href="/wiki/Fender_Telecaster" title="Fender Telecaster">Fender Telecaster</a> and the unique mix with the traditional country <a href="/wiki/Steel_guitar" title="Steel guitar">steel guitar</a> sound, new vocal harmony styles in which the words are minimal, and a rough edge not heard on the more polished <a href="/wiki/Nashville_sound" title="Nashville sound">Nashville sound</a> recordings of the same era.</p> 
     <p>Haggard's childhood was troubled after the death of his father, and he was incarcerated several times in his youth. He managed to turn his life around and launch a successful country music career, gaining popularity with his songs about the working class that occasionally contained themes contrary to the prevailing anti-<a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> subject matter of much popular music of the time. Between the 1960s and the 1980s, he had 38 number one hits on the US country charts, several of which also made the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> all-genre singles chart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-haggardsongdb_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-haggardsongdb-1">[1]</a></sup> During the 1970s, Haggard became aligned with the growing <a href="/wiki/Outlaw_country" title="Outlaw country">outlaw country</a> movement, and he continued to release successful albums through the 1990s and into the 2000s.</p> 
     <p>He received many honors and awards for his music, including a <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Center_Honors" title="Kennedy Center Honors">Kennedy Center Honor</a> (2010), a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award" title="Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award">Grammy Lifetime Achievement Award</a> (2006), a <a href="/wiki/BMI_Awards" title="BMI Awards">BMI Icon Award</a> (2006),<sup id="cite_ref-bmiawards_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmiawards-2">[2]</a></sup> and induction into the <a href="/wiki/Nashville_Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame" title="Nashville Songwriters Hall of Fame">Nashville Songwriters Hall of Fame</a> (1977),<sup id="cite_ref-nashvillehof_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nashvillehof-3">[3]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Hall_of_Fame_and_Museum" title="Country Music Hall of Fame and Museum">Country Music Hall of Fame</a> (1994)<sup id="cite_ref-countrymusichof_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-countrymusichof-4">[4]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Oklahoma_Music_Hall_of_Fame" title="Oklahoma Music Hall of Fame">Oklahoma Music Hall of Fame</a> (1997).<sup id="cite_ref-okmusichof_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-okmusichof-5">[5]</a></sup> He died on April 6, 2016 — his 79th birthday — at his ranch in Northern California, having recently suffered from <a href="/wiki/Pneumonia" title="Pneumonia">pneumonia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nytobit_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytobit-6">[6]</a></sup></p> 
     <p></p>
