      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>As noted by a <i><a href="/wiki/Washington_Post" title="Washington Post" class="mw-redirect">Washington Post</a></i> article published upon Haggard's death, "Respect for the Hag [Haggard] as an icon, both for his musical status and his personal views, is a common theme" in country music.<sup id="cite_ref-yahr_80-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahr-80">[80]</a></sup> Many country music acts have paid tribute to Haggard by mentioning him in their songs. These include:</p> 
     <ul> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Dixie_Chicks" title="Dixie Chicks">The Dixie Chicks</a> paid tribute to Haggard by recording <a href="/wiki/Darrell_Scott" title="Darrell Scott">Darrell Scott</a>'s song "Long Time Gone", which criticizes Nashville trends: "We listen to the radio to hear what's cookin’/But the music ain't got no soul/ Now they sound tired but they don’t sound Haggard", with the following lines mentioning <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash" title="Johnny Cash">Johnny Cash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hank_Williams" title="Hank Williams">Hank Williams</a> in the same vein.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/Collin_Raye" title="Collin Raye">Collin Raye</a> recorded "My Kind of Girl", which includes the line "How 'bout some music/She said have you got any Merle/That's when I knew she was my kind of girl".<sup id="cite_ref-yahr_80-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahr-80">[80]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>In 2000, Alan Jackson and George Strait sang "Murder on Music Row", which criticizes mainstream country trends: "The Hag wouldn't have a chance on today's radio/Because they committed murder down on music row".<sup id="cite_ref-yahr_80-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahr-80">[80]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>In 2005, the country rock duo <a href="/wiki/Brooks_%26_Dunn" title="Brooks &amp; Dunn">Brooks &amp; Dunn</a> sang "Just Another Neon Night" off their Hillbilly Deluxe album. In the song, <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Dunn" title="Ronnie Dunn">Ronnie Dunn</a> said "He's got an Eastwood grin and a too early swagger/Hollerin' turn off that rap/And play me some Haggard". Brooks &amp; Dunn also reference Haggard in 1993's "Rock My World (little country girl)" off their Hard Workin' Man Album as they sing "Acts like <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> but she listens to Merle/Rock my world little country girl".<sup id="cite_ref-yahr_80-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahr-80">[80]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Red Simpson mentions Haggard and Buck Owens in his 1971 song "I'm a Truck", which contains the line, "Well, I know what he's gonna do now/Take out that tape cartridge of Buck Owens and play it again/I dunno why he don't get a Merle Haggard Tape".<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>In 2005, <a href="/wiki/Shooter_Jennings" title="Shooter Jennings">Shooter Jennings</a> mentioned Haggard in the title track of his album <i><a href="/wiki/Put_the_%22O%22_Back_in_Country" title="Put the &quot;O&quot; Back in Country">Put the "O" Back in Country</a></i> and later mentioned him in 2007 in his song "Concrete Cowboys".<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>In 2006, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Williams_III" title="Hank Williams III">Hank Williams III</a> included Haggard as well as other country icons in the song "Country Heroes".<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/LeAnn_Rimes" title="LeAnn Rimes">LeAnn Rimes</a> mentions him in her 2013 song, <i>I Do Now</i>: “Thank God for Merle Haggard, he’s right, the bottle let me down.”<sup id="cite_ref-yahr_80-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahr-80">[80]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>"<a href="/wiki/You_Never_Even_Called_Me_by_My_Name" title="You Never Even Called Me by My Name">You Never Even Called Me by My Name</a>" mentions Haggard alongside Waylon Jennings and <a href="/wiki/Charley_Pride" title="Charley Pride">Charley Pride</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup></li> 
      <li><a href="/wiki/George_Jones" title="George Jones">George Jones</a> mentions "The Okie from Muskogee" in his song "Who's Gonna Fill Their Shoes".<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>Gretchen Wilson's song "Politically Uncorrect" and Eric Church's song "I Pledge Allegiance to the Hag" both contain tributes to Haggard, as well as featuring him as a guest vocalist.<sup id="cite_ref-yahr_80-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yahr-80">[80]</a></sup></li> 
      <li>The Lexington Lab Band in 2013 recorded four videos of Haggard songs, also performing several of those songs in 2014 and again in 2015, in live tribute shows at the Lyric Theatre in Lexington, Kentucky.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></li> 
     </ul> 
     <p>In the 1970s, several rock acts responded in their own songs to Haggard's criticism of hippie counterculture in "Okie from Muskogee" and "The Fightin' Side of Me". <a href="/wiki/The_Youngbloods" title="The Youngbloods">The Youngbloods</a> answered "Okie from Muskogee" with "Hippie from Olema", in which, in one repetition of the chorus, they change the line "We still take in strangers if they're ragged" to "We still take in strangers if they're haggard".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECantwell.2C_David2013174_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECantwell.2C_David2013174-114">[114]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nick_Gravenites" title="Nick Gravenites">Nick Gravenites</a>, of <a href="/wiki/Big_Brother_and_the_Holding_Company" title="Big Brother and the Holding Company">Big Brother and the Holding Company</a>, paid Haggard a tongue-in-cheek tribute with the song, "I'll Change Your Flat Tire, Merle",<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> later covered by other artists including <a href="/wiki/Pure_Prairie_League" title="Pure Prairie League">Pure Prairie League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> Despite these critiques, the Grateful Dead performed "Mama Tried" over 300 times,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> and "Sing Me Back Home" approximately 40 times.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Southern_rock" title="Southern rock">Southern rock</a> band <a href="/wiki/Lynyrd_Skynyrd" title="Lynyrd Skynyrd">Lynyrd Skynyrd</a> more respectfully referenced Haggard in their song, "<a href="/wiki/Nuthin%27_Fancy" title="Nuthin' Fancy">Railroad Song</a>", which contains the lyric, "Well I'm a ride this train Lord until I find out/What <a href="/wiki/Jimmie_Rodgers_(country_singer)" title="Jimmie Rodgers (country singer)">Jimmie Rodgers</a> and the Hag was all about". Skynyrd also performed both a cover of "<a href="/wiki/Merle_Haggard_Presents_His_30th_Album" title="Merle Haggard Presents His 30th Album">Honky Tonk Night Time Man</a>" as well as their own take on the song with "Jacksonville Kid" (found on the 2001 CD reissue of the album) on their album <i><a href="/wiki/Street_Survivors" title="Street Survivors">Street Survivors</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Discography">Discography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Merle_Haggard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Discography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Merle_Haggard&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
     <div> 
      <table style="width: 100%; background-color:transparent;table-layout:fixed; border:none; border-spacing:0;" role="presentation"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr style="vertical-align: top;"> 
         <td> 
          <div style="margin-right:20px;"> 
           <p><b><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1965 Most Promising Male Vocalist</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1965 Best Vocal Group</a> – <small>with <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Owens" title="Bonnie Owens">Bonnie Owens</a></small></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1965 Top Vocal Group</a> <small>with <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Owens" title="Bonnie Owens">Bonnie Owens</a></small></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1966 Top Male Vocalist</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1967 Top Duo</a> <small>with <a href="/wiki/Bonnie_Owens" title="Bonnie Owens">Bonnie Owens</a></small></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1969 Top Male Vocalist</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1969 Album of the Year</a> – "<a href="/wiki/Okie_from_Muskogee" title="Okie from Muskogee">Okie from Muskogee</a>"</li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1969 Song of the Year</a> – "<a href="/wiki/Okie_from_Muskogee_(song)" title="Okie from Muskogee (song)">Okie from Muskogee</a>"</li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1969 Single of the Year</a> – "<a href="/wiki/Okie_from_Muskogee_(song)" title="Okie from Muskogee (song)">Okie from Muskogee</a>"</li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1970 Entertainer of the Year</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1970 Top Male Vocalist</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1972 Top Male Vocalist</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1974 Top Male Vocalist</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1981 Top Male Vocalist</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1982 Song of the Year</a> – "<a href="/wiki/Are_the_Good_Times_Really_Over_(I_Wish_a_Buck_Was_Still_Silver)" title="Are the Good Times Really Over (I Wish a Buck Was Still Silver)">Are the Good Times Really Over</a>" (won award as both artist and composer)</li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">1995 Pioneer Award</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">2005 Triple Crown</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">2008 Poet's Award</a></li> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">2013 Crystal Milestone Award</a></li> 
           </ul> 
           <p><b><a href="/wiki/BMI_Awards" title="BMI Awards">BMI Awards</a></b></p> 
           <ul> 
            <li>2006 BMI Icon Award<sup id="cite_ref-bmiawards_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bmiawards-2">[2]</a></sup></li> 
           </ul> 
          </div> </td>

            <li><a href="/wiki/Country_Music_Association_Awards" title="Country Music Association Awards">1983 Vocal Duo of the Year</a> – <small>with <a href="/wiki/Willie_Nelson" title="Willie Nelson">Willie Nelson</a></small></li>
